        <span class="sh-eyebrow">About Me</span>

        <h2 class="sh-h2">Hi, I'm Sharaheel — or Shar for short.</h2>

        <p class="sh-lead">I'm a Computer Science student at the University of Illinois Chicago building toward cybersecurity, Security Analyst roles, and technical problem-solving. This portfolio documents what I'm learning, what I'm building, and how I think through problems.</p>

<div class="sh-about-grid">

        <div class="sh-about-card sh-reveal">

          <div class="sh-kix">Builder by Curiosity</div>

          <h3>I learn by building.</h3>

          <p>I like turning ideas into low-stakes prototypes I can test and improve — a Calendar AI assistant, a chess minigame, and this WordPress portfolio. Shipping something small teaches me more than reading about it.</p>

        </div>

        <div class="sh-about-card sh-reveal">

          <div class="sh-kix">Competitive by Nature</div>

          <h3>Focus under pressure.</h3>

          <p>I'm a 1700 Elo, state-level chess player, and I play CS, Valorant, and Fortnite. Competition taught me focus, fast adaptation, and how to learn from losses instead of avoiding them.</p>

        </div>

        <div class="sh-about-card sh-reveal">

          <div class="sh-kix">Building Toward Cybersecurity</div>

          <h3>A clear target.</h3>

          <p>Through the Google Cybersecurity Certificate and CodePath I've studied Linux, SQL, SIEM, threat modeling, vulnerability assessment, and incident response. I'm targeting a Security Analyst path, with Network+ and Security+ next.</p>

      <!-- TIMELY AI -->

      <article class="sh-proj sh-reveal" id="p-timely">

        <div class="sh-proj-top">

          <div>

            <span class="sh-eyebrow">Featured Project</span>

            <h3 class="sh-proj-title">Timely AI Calendar Assistant</h3>

            <p class="sh-proj-text">Timely AI is a calendar assistant I built to help users manage their schedule through natural language. The app connects to Google Calendar, displays events in a clean calendar dashboard, and includes an AI chat assistant that can answer schedule questions, check availability, and help create meetings.</p>

            <p class="sh-proj-text">This project demonstrates AI-assisted development, interface design, scheduling logic, and user-focused functionality.</p>

            <div class="sh-tags">

              <span class="sh-tag">AI Assistant</span>

              <span class="sh-tag">Google Calendar</span>

              <span class="sh-tag">Scheduling</span>

            </div>

          </div>

          <div class="sh-highlight">

            <h4>What this project shows</h4>

            <ul>

              <li>Calendar dashboard with visible events</li>

              <li>AI chat panel for schedule questions</li>

              <li>Natural-language scheduling and availability checks</li>

              <li>Cleaner UI through testing and iteration</li>

              <li>Responsible AI use as a development support tool</li>

            </ul>

          </div>

        </div>

      <!-- AIM TRAINER -->

      <article class="sh-proj sh-reveal" id="p-aim">

        <div class="sh-proj-top">

          <div>

            <span class="sh-eyebrow">Interactive App Project</span>

            <h3 class="sh-proj-title">Aim Trainer Reaction Game</h3>

            <p class="sh-proj-text">This Aim Trainer is a simple reaction-based desktop app I built to help users practice speed, accuracy, and consistency. The user clicks randomly placed targets while the app tracks points, streaks, average reaction time, and time remaining.</p>

            <p class="sh-proj-text">I kept the design intentionally clean and focused. The app includes a settings menu where users can switch between Simple and Stats mode, choose 30-second, 60-second, or Infinite play, and pause the game without losing the visual style of the app.</p>

            <div class="sh-tags">

              <span class="sh-tag">Reaction Game</span>

              <span class="sh-tag">UI Design</span>

              <span class="sh-tag">Performance Tracking</span>

              <span class="sh-tag">Electron App</span>

            </div>

          </div>

          <div class="sh-highlight">

            <h4>What this project shows</h4>

            <ul>

              <li>Interactive target-clicking game logic</li>

              <li>Points, streaks, and average reaction tracking</li>

              <li>Simple and Stats display modes</li>

              <li>30-second, 60-second, and Infinite timer options</li>

              <li>Clean settings menu and pause overlay</li>

            </ul>

          </div>

        </div>


        <figure class="sh-media">

          <iframe class="sh-video" src="https://videopress.com/embed/Z3zz4yOi?cover=1&amp;preloadContent=metadata&amp;useAverageColor=true" allowfullscreen></iframe>

          <div class="sh-proof-card"><h4>Solution</h4><p>I built a clean aim trainer with targets, scoring, streaks, timers, and a simple settings menu.</p></div>

          <div class="sh-proof-card"><h4>Design Choice</h4><p>I kept the interface minimal so the game feels easy to understand and quick to play.</p></div>

          <div class="sh-proof-card"><h4>What I Learned</h4><p>This helped me practice interactive UI logic, state management, timing, and user-focused design.</p></div>

      <!-- MATE IN 10 -->

      <article class="sh-proj sh-reveal" id="p-mate">

        <div class="sh-proj-top">

          <div>

            <span class="sh-eyebrow">CS 111 Exemplary Project</span>

            <h3 class="sh-proj-title">Mate in 10! Chess Puzzle Minigame</h3>

            <p class="sh-proj-text">Mate in 10! was my CS 111 final project, built with Python Turtle. The game starts with a Learn Mode that teaches chess piece movement, then moves into a 10-puzzle practice run where users solve tactics from easy to hard.</p>

            <p class="sh-proj-text">My group earned an exemplary grade on this project. It shows my ability to build a larger interactive Python program with visual design, event handling, game logic, feedback, scoring, timing, and a polished user flow.</p>

            <div class="sh-tags">

              <span class="sh-tag">Python Turtle</span>

              <span class="sh-tag">Game Logic</span>

              <span class="sh-tag">UI Design</span>

              <span class="sh-tag">Exemplary Grade</span>

            </div>

          </div>

          <div class="sh-highlight">

            <h4>What this project shows</h4>

            <ul>

              <li>Interactive Python Turtle interface</li>

              <li>Learn Mode for chess movement practice</li>

              <li>10-puzzle run with tactics and difficulty progression</li>

              <li>Timer, misclicks, clean solves, and best-run tracking</li>

              <li>Clear feedback screens and replay options</li>

            </ul>

          </div>

        </div>

  <!-- ============ 6. CYBERSECURITY ============ -->

  <section class="sh-section sh-band" id="security" data-screen-label="Cybersecurity">

    <div class="sh-wrap">

      <div class="sh-reveal">

        <span class="sh-eyebrow">Cybersecurity</span>

        <h2 class="sh-h2">My Cybersecurity Learning Notes</h2>

        <p class="sh-lead">Security matters to my path because I keep asking the same three questions about any system: what could go wrong, who's affected, and what's the safer path? These notes track what I'm studying as I work toward a Security Analyst role.</p>

      </div>

      <div class="sh-cyber-grid">

        <div class="sh-studied sh-reveal">

          <h3>What I've Studied</h3>

          <div class="sh-studied-list">

            <div class="sh-studied-item"><b>Linux</b><span>Command line, permissions, and navigating a system the way an analyst does.</span></div>

            <div class="sh-studied-item"><b>SQL</b><span>Querying data and understanding how databases can be probed or misused.</span></div>

            <div class="sh-studied-item"><b>SIEM</b><span>Reading logs and alerts to spot what looks normal versus suspicious.</span></div>

            <div class="sh-studied-item"><b>Threat Modeling</b><span>Mapping what could go wrong before it does, and where the weak points are.</span></div>

            <div class="sh-studied-item"><b>Incident Response</b><span>Knowing the steps to take when something does go wrong.</span></div>

            <div class="sh-studied-item"><b>Vulnerability Assessment</b><span>Looking for gaps and weaknesses in a system on purpose.</span></div>

            <div class="sh-studied-item" style="grid-column:1 / -1;"><b>Defensive Security</b><span>Thinking like a defender — protecting users, data, and access instead of just reacting.</span></div>

          </div>

        </div>

        <div class="sh-cyber-side">

          <div class="sh-side-card sh-reveal">

            <h4>Security + AI Ethics</h4>

            <p>I treat AI as a helper, not a source of truth. I verify what it gives me, and I never paste private or sensitive data into a tool I don't control. Responsible use is part of security.</p>

          </div>

          <div class="sh-side-card sh-reveal">

            <h4>What I'm Building Toward</h4>

            <p>I want to grow into support and deeper cybersecurity work, carrying a verification mindset into everything — checking assumptions, confirming details, and protecting the people behind the system.</p>

          </div>

        </div>

      </div>

    </div>

  </section>


  <!-- ============ 7. AI JOURNEY ============ -->

  <section class="sh-section" id="ai-journey" data-screen-label="AI Journey">

    <div class="sh-wrap">

      <div class="sh-reveal">

        <span class="sh-eyebrow">AI + Verification Workflow</span>

        <h2 class="sh-h2">AI is a thinking tool, not a judgment replacement.</h2>

        <p class="sh-lead">I use AI to think and document more clearly, never to replace my own judgment. I care about accuracy over speed, which means the work isn't done until I've checked it.</p>

      </div>

      <div class="sh-journey-grid">

        <div class="sh-journey-card sh-reveal">

          <div class="sh-num">01</div>

          <h3>How I Use AI</h3>

          <ul>

            <li>Brainstorm and explore approaches before building</li>

            <li>Organize messy notes and next steps</li>

            <li>Clarify concepts I'm still learning</li>

            <li>Improve how I communicate and explain my work</li>

          </ul>

        </div>

        <div class="sh-journey-card sh-reveal">

          <div class="sh-num">02</div>

          <h3>Verification in Practice</h3>

          <p>In Timely AI, a user types a request in natural language and the app turns it into a Google Calendar event. Before anything is created, it checks for missing details and asks the user to confirm — AI proposes, the human decides.</p>

        </div>

        <div class="sh-journey-card sh-reveal">

          <div class="sh-num">03</div>

          <h3>Why This Matters for My Path</h3>

          <p>Cybersecurity and support work both depend on not trusting things blindly. The same habit — check the claim, confirm the detail, keep a human in the loop — is exactly what I want to carry into my career.</p>

        </div>

        <div class="sh-journey-card sh-reveal">

          <div class="sh-num">04</div>

          <h3>The Loop</h3>

          <p><strong>Brainstorm → Build → Verify.</strong> I move fast with AI in the first two steps, then slow down to confirm important claims through documentation, testing, logs, or my own reasoning before I trust the output.</p>

        </div>

      </div>

    </div>

  </section>

    <span class="sh-ps-eyebrow">Personal Statement</span>

    <h2 class="sh-ps-title" id="sh-ps-title">What I build, and where I'm headed.</h2>

    <div class="sh-ps-body">

      <p>I build AI systems people can trust with their real data. The demo version of that is easy: point a language model at a task and it'll usually look impressive. The hard version is getting it to behave correctly when it's writing to someone's live calendar. That's the work I care about.</p>

      <p>Timely AI is where I proved I could do it. It's an agentic scheduling assistant — React on the front end, Flask on the back. Instead of letting the model free-form a reply, I have it sort each request into one of five intent types, and then a deterministic validation step checks that output before anything gets written. It catches scheduling conflicts, and it won't commit a change until the user confirms. To see whether the whole thing held together, I built a scored eval harness across 13 input categories. It came in at 98% accuracy, and once I reworked how intents were handled, cancel requests jumped from 33% correct to 100%. I have the eval results to back that up.</p>

      <p>I also know what I still need to build. Much of my strongest work has leaned on AI assistance, so right now I'm putting real time into the fundamentals I want to own on my own, mainly the math and statistics under machine learning. My fall courses, Applied Linear Algebra and Applied Statistical Methods, go straight at it. And since I've built most things solo, I'm getting fluent with team version control and code review on GitHub now, before it counts on the job.</p>

      <p>What I want next is an AI engineering internship for Summer 2027, ideally at a place shipping real AI products rather than a chatbot bolted onto an existing app. After I finish my CS degree at UIC in 2029, I want to do this full-time: building AI systems people can depend on.</p>

    </div>

  </div>

</div>

</div>
